        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous hybrid materials with designed micro/nano-sub-structures have been recognized as promising anodes for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their high capacity and reliable performance.  The low elec. cond. and side-reactions at the interface of electrode/electrolyte prohibit their practical applications.  Carbon material modification can effectively enhance the cond. and mech. properties, and suppress the direct contact between the electrode and electrolyte, leading to enhanced performance.  Herein, unique porous MnO with micro/nano-architectures has been in situ decorated with carbon layers on the surface and by carbon nanotube doping between the particles (denoted as MnO@C/CNTs) by a catalytic chem. vapor deposition (CCVD) treatment.  As anodes in LIBs, these MnO@C/CNTs exhibit remarkable cycling performance (1266 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and good rate capability (850 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1).  The inspiring performance is assocd. with the carbon modified porous micro/nano-structure features which can buffer the vol. expansion and promote the ion/electron transfer at the interface of electrode/electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpK1Oxo39q8WrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhp6IoUs4yItA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFOqtrbF&amp;md5=97c52c68651b2c7cec918b1f7d9a7c6b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201605820"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Confined Amorphous Red Phosphorus in MOF-Derived N-Doped Microporous Carbon as a Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved electrochemical performance of boron-doped carbon-coated lithium titanate as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yun, Bin-Na; Du, Hoang Long; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Jung, Hun-Gi; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A B-doped C layer (BC) was coated on porous micron-sized Li4Ti5O12 (LTO) via a facile wet-chem. method for use as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries.  As detd. by x-ray photoemission spectroscopy and Raman spectroscopy, 3 different species (BC3, BC2O, and BCO2) were doped in the C layer on the surface of LTO.  These heteroatoms lead to abundant extrinsic defects in the C layer that result in improved Na-ion diffusivity across the active material.  Using electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, the diffusion coeff. of the B-doped C-coated LTO (BC-LTO) is 2.241 × 10-15 cm2 s-1.  The BC-LTO exhibited 85% and 60% higher Na-ion diffusivity than pristine LTO and C-coated LTO (C-LTO), resp.  Also, electron-deficient B in BC3 enhances the elec. cond. through pos. charged holes that carry electrons through the C structure.  Accordingly, the BC-LTO electrode showed a high specific capacity of 148 mA-h g-1 at 0.5 C and 98.4 mA-h g-1 at 10C rate.  The BC-LTO anode demonstrated a great capacity retention of ∼90% at 1 and 10C after 300 cycles.  These findings demonstrate the promising potential of LTO as a high-performance anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgDus9NKdbdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCUGZ3jDBlsA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFCgt73F&amp;md5=242e1f1fc5d3bb47237faa2b2f76e571</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201104634"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Noble metal nanoparticles (MNPs) have attracted continuous attention due to their promising applications in chem., physics, bioscience, medicine and materials science.  As an alternative to conventional soln. chem. routes, MNPs can be directly synthesized through a conjugated polymer (CP) mediated technique utilizing the redox chem. of CPs to chem. reduce the metal ions and modulate the size, morphol., and structure of the MNPs.  The as-prepd. multifunctional CP-MNP nanocomposites have shown application potentials as highly sensitive surface enhanced Raman spectroscopy (SERS) substrates, effective heterogeneous catalysts for org. synthesis and electrochem., and key components for electronic and sensing devices.  In this tutorial review, we begin with a brief introduction to the chem. nature and redox properties of CPs that enable the spontaneous redn. of noble metal ions to form MNPs.  We then focus on recent progress in control over the size, morphol. and structure of MNPs during the conjugated polymer mediated syntheses of CP-MNP nanocomposites.  Finally, we highlight the multifunctional CP-MNP nanocomposites toward their applications in sensing, catalysis, and electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8wtExX8CyjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh500J6R7HWAQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFWhsL4%253D&amp;md5=20e27af37db3db6c6b0b766ef3706f3f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.3390/polym8100366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heteroatom-Doped Carbon Nanostructures Derived from Conjugated Polymers for Energy Applications</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Polymers</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">366</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heteroatom-doped carbon nanostructures derived from conjugated polymers for energy applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Yanzhen; Han, Xijiang; Du, Yunchen; Zhang, Bin; Xu, Ping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Polymers (Basel, Switzerland)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doped carbon materials have been one of the most remarkable families of materials with promising applications in fuel cells, supercapacitors, and batteries.  Among them, conjugated polymer (CP)-derived heteroatom-doped carbon materials exhibit remarkable electrochem. performances because the heteroatoms can be preserved at a relatively high content and keep stable under harsh working conditions.  In this review, we summarized recent advances in the rational design and various applications of CP-derived heteroatom-doped carbon materials, including polyaniline (PANI), polypyrrole (PPy), and their ramification-derived carbons, as well as transition metal-carbon nanocomposites.  The key point of considering CP-derived heteroatom-doped carbon materials as important candidates of electrode materials is that CPs contain only nonmetallic elements and some key heteroatoms in their backbones which provide great chances for the synthesis of metal-free heteroatom-doped carbon nanostructures.  The presented examples in this review will provide new insights in designing and optimizing heteroatom-doped carbon materials for the development of anode and cathode materials for electrochem. device applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonB3tEb8RIerVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh500J6R7HWAQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktlajurc%253D&amp;md5=ae545e13ffccccc410d917cff8a72892</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1021/ja402450a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Silva, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Voiry, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chhowalla, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Asefa, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Metal-Free Electrocatalysts for Oxygen Reduction: Polyaniline-Derived N- and O-doped Mesoporous Carbons</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient metal-free electrocatalysts for oxygen reduction: polyaniline-derived N- and O-doped mesoporous carbons</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Silva, Rafael; Voiry, Damien; Chhowalla, Manish; Asefa, Tewodros</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The oxygen redn. reaction (ORR)-one of the two half-reactions in fuel cells-is one of the bottlenecks that has prevented fuel cells from finding a wide range of applications today.  This is because ORR is inherently a sluggish reaction; it is also because inexpensive and sustainable ORR electrocatalysts that are not only efficient but also are based on earth-abundant elements are hard to come by.  Herein we report the synthesis of novel carbon-based materials that can contribute to solving these challenges assocd. with ORR.  Mesoporous oxygen- and nitrogen-doped carbons were synthesized from in situ polymd. mesoporous silica-supported polyaniline (PANI) by carbonization of the latter, followed by etching away the mesoporous silica template from it.  The synthetic method also allowed the immobilization of different metals such as Fe and Co easily into the system.  While all the resulting materials showed outstanding electrocatalytic activity toward ORR, the metal-free, PANI-derived mesoporous carbon (dubbed PDMC), in particular, exhibited the highest activity, challenging conventional paradigms.  This unprecedented activity by the metal-free PDMC toward ORR was attributed to the synergetic activities of nitrogen and oxygen (or hydroxyl) species that were implanted in it by PANI/mesoporous silica during pyrolysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqu_zhHIpLhBrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh500J6R7HWAQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXntVOkurw%253D&amp;md5=f05c2e7c88034ee0359818cc8846c53b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.5b00292"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qi, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Shape Fixing via Salt Recrystallization: A Morphology-Controlled Approach To Convert Nanostructured Polymer to Carbon Nanomaterial as a Highly Active Catalyst for Oxygen Reduction Reaction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Shape Fixing via Salt Recrystallization: A Morphology-Controlled Approach To Convert Nanostructured Polymer to Carbon Nanomaterial as a Highly Active Catalyst for Oxygen Reduction Reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Wei; Li, Li; Xiong, Kun; Wang, Yao; Li, Wei; Nie, Yao; Chen, Siguo; Qi, Xueqiang; Wei, Zidong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, the authors report a shape fixing via salt recrystn. method to efficiently synthesize N-doped C material with a large no. of active sites exposed to the 3-phase zones, for use as an ORR catalyst.  Self-assembled polyaniline with a 3-dimensional network structure was fixed and fully sealed inside NaCl via recrystn. of NaCl soln.  During pyrolysis, the NaCl crystal functions as a fully sealed nanoreactor, which facilitates N incorporation and graphitization.  The gasification in such a closed nanoreactor creates a large no. of pores in the resultant samples.  The 3-dimensional network structure, which is conducive to mass transport and high use of active sites, has been accurately transferred to the final N-doped C materials, after dissoln. of the NaCl.  Use of the invented cathode catalyst in a p exchange membrane fuel cell produces a peak power of 600 mW cm-2, making this among the best nonprecious metal catalysts for the ORR reported so far.  Also, N-doped C materials with a nanotube or nanoshell morphol. can be realized by the invented method.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsQl3xFu0k3bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh500J6R7HWAQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmsVSksb8%253D&amp;md5=8123237e8236fe4806a4e20b2855eca1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b07865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bifunctional Nitrogen-Doped Microporous Carbon Microspheres Derived from Poly(o-methylaniline) for Oxygen Reduction and Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bifunctional Nitrogen-Doped Microporous Carbon Microspheres Derived from Poly(o-methylaniline) for Oxygen Reduction and Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Yanzhen; Han, Xijiang; Du, Yunchen; Song, Bo; Xu, Ping; Zhang, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

Here the authors demonstrate a facile poly(o-methylaniline)-derived fabrication of bifunctional microporous N-doped C microspheres (NCMSs) with high electrocatalytic activity and stability for ORR and energy storage in supercapacitors.  At a pyrolysis temp. of 900°, the highly dispersed NCMSs present a high surface area (727.1 m2 g-1), proper total content of doping N, and high concn. of quaternary N, which exhibit superior electrocatalytic activities for ORR to the com.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Fiber Supercapacitor with High Energy Density Based on Hollow Graphene/Conducting Polymer Fiber Electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Guoxing; Cheng, Jianli; Li, Xiaodong; Yuan, Demao; Chen, Peining; Chen, Xuli; Wang, Bin; Peng, Huisheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow fiber electrodes were developed to fabricate novel and high-performance fiber-shaped supercapacitors.  The fiber supercapacitors based on the hollow composite fiber had an ultra-high specific capacitance of 304.5 mF cm-2 (8.1 mF/cm, 143.3 F/cm3 or 63.1 F/g), which is 2-8 times of the other fiber-shaped supercapacitors.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped hierarchically porous carbon as efficient oxygen reduction electrocatalysts in acid electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhong, Hexiang; Deng, Chengwei; Qiu, Yanling; Yao, Lan; Zhang, Huamin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17047-17057</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped carbon was found to exhibit excellent activity as an electrocatalyst in renewable energy devices.  A controllable method to synthesize N-doped hierarchically porous carbons (PNCEs) partly with graphene-like structure using polyaniline (PANI)-polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP) composite as a carbon source via a soft-template process was reported.  The catalytic mechanism was thoroughly studied to better understand the relationship between the structure, Fe species and catalytic activity.  The PNCE prepd. at 1000°C displays the best performance achieving a max. power d. of 456 mW/cm2 and oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) onset potential of 0.90 V.  More prominently, the catalyst presents superior stability, as well as poison tolerance including methanol and SO2 to the com. JM-Pt/C catalyst in 0.5 M H2SO4.  The PVP is proven to tailor the structure, improve the surface area, and alter the transition metal species.  The PNCEs synthesized under NH3 exhibit considerably better catalytic activity toward ORR compared with the undoped carbon and PNCEs synthesized under an N2 atmosphere.  Furthermore, we find that the nitrogen bonding configurations, textural structure, Fe species and surface areas of PNCEs play key roles in the electrocatalytic activity towards the ORR.  The formed FeN4 species hosted in the micropores acts as the active component for ORR activity in PNCEs, although it is not the only contributor to the high performance of PNCEs.  The catalyst is expected to be a promising non-noble electrocatalyst for use in polymer electrolyte membrane fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdGZbXDYNSQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9qfFcCO1wgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlOjsbjM&amp;md5=9e9d9f5cf9573fca03733f0ed560f927</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">27</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">6702</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">62074</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6702-6707</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small Sn nanodots (1-2 nm) were delicately encapsulated in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers through electrospinning and thermal treatment.  The size and content of Sn particles can be controlled by changing reaction conditions.  When evaluated as binder- and current collector-free anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries, Sn NDs@PNC nanofibers delivered a reversible capacity of 633 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More impressively, a capacity of 450 mA h g-1 even at 10 000 mA g-1 and 483 mA h g-1 over 1300 cycles at 2000 mA g-1 were achieved.  To our knowledge, this is the highest rate performance and cyclic stability of tin for Na storage.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of Sn NDs@PNC is attributed to the following: First, the ultra-small Sn NDs (1-2 nm) decreases the abs. strain and improve the utilization rate of active materials during sodiation/de-sodiation process; second, the uniform distribution of Sn NDs in the fibrous carbon matrix is an important factor to generate a balanced stress over the whole composite with maintaining the integrity of the electrode upon prolonged cycling; third, the 1D porous N-doped carbon frame can interlink into a 3D conductive network, which facilitates the electron and Na+ diffusion kinetics and buffers the large vol. fluctuation of Sn NDs and prevents their pulverization and aggregation.  Carbon fibers also serve as both current collector and conductive material - this avoids the common loss of electrochem. contact between the active materials and the current collector/conductive additives, and reduces the inactive wt. and vol. of cells thus improving the energy d.  This simple and scalable synthesis as well as the promising electrochem. performance encourages application of Sn-based materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnXAQ9MCRr0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9qfFcCO1wgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ks77J&amp;md5=c6f2a6fad6ab6e844a9149e974f0edf1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA04366B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ruan, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chou, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorus/N-Doped Carbon Nanofiber Composite as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been attracting intensive attention at present as the most promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries in large-scale elec. energy storage applications, due to the low-cost and natural abundance of sodium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is a very promising anode material for SIBs, with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  Recently, there have been many efforts devoted to phosphorus anode materials for SIBs.  As pure red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly, many attempts to prep. composite materials contg. phosphorus have been reported.  Here, we report the facile prepn. of a red phosphorus/N-doped carbon nanofiber composite (P/NCF) that can deliver a reversible capacity of 731 mA h g-1 in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), with a capacity retention of 57.3% over 55 cycles.  Our results suggest that it would be a promising anode candidate for SIBs with a high capacity and low cost.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0NKI079Ynj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9qfFcCO1wgw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1yqtbnL&amp;md5=a7f25f4a70413c0ff39a5df24c5ffca6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/marc.200500514"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dai, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Fabrication of Functional Polypyrrole Nanotubes via a Reactive Self-Degraded Template</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Macromol.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Asymmetric Supercapacitor Based on Structure-Optimized Mn3O4/Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanohybrid Paper with High Energy and Power Density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Yating; Guan, Cao; Feng, Guangxue; Ke, Qingqing; Huang, Xiaolei; Wang, John</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A highly flexible Mn3O4/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanohybrid paper with high elec. cond. and high mass loading of Mn3O4 nanofibers (0.71 g cm-3) is developed via a facile gel formation and electrochem. redn. process, which is low-cost, environmental friendly, and easy to scale up.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Active MnOx electrocatalysts prepared by atomic layer deposition for oxygen evolution and oxygen reduction reactions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pickrahn, Katie L.; Park, Sang Wook; Gorlin, Yelena; Lee, Han-Bo-Ram; Jaramillo, Thomas F.; Bent, Stacey F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ability to deposit conformal catalytic thin films enables opportunities to achieve complex nanostructured designs for catalysis.  Atomic layer deposition (ALD) is capable of creating conformal thin films over complex substrates.  Here, ALD-MnOx on glassy C was studied as a catalyst for the O evolution reaction (OER) and the O redn. reaction (ORR), two reactions that are of growing interest due to their many applications in alternative energy technologies.  The films were characterized by XPS, x-ray diffraction, SEM, ellipsometry, and cyclic voltammetry.  The as-deposited films consist of Mn(II)O, which is a poor catalyst for the ORR, but highly active for the OER.  By controllably annealing the samples, Mn2O3 catalysts with good activity for both the ORR and OER were synthesized.  Hypotheses are presented to explain the large difference in the activity between the MnO and Mn2O3 catalysts for the ORR, but similar activity for the OER, including the effects of surface oxidn. under exptl. conditions.  These catalysts synthesized though ALD compare favorably to the best MnOx catalysts in the literature, demonstrating a viable way to produce highly active, conformal thin films from earth-abundant materials for the ORR and the OER.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCHku0Ms9RorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhBu4T_-g982g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFSmsLfO&amp;md5=77e61520524a8847d31c67b62c0e8eb9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201604108"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">S-Doped N-Rich Carbon Nanosheets with Expanded Interlayer Distance as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn nanoparticles embedded in nitrogen-doped porous carbon as high-performance anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Zhiqiang; Wang, Shiwen; Du, Jing; Jin, Qi; Zhang, Tianran; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report on the prepn. and Li ion battery anode application of ultrasmall Sn nanoparticles (∼5 nm) embedded in nitrogen-doped porous carbon network (denoted as 5-Sn/C).  Pyrolysis of Sn-(Salen) at 650°C under Ar atm. was carried out to prep. N-doped porous 5-Sn/C with the BET sp. surface area of 286.3 m2 g-1.  The 5-Sn/C showed an initial discharge capacity of 1014 mAh g-1 and a capacity retention of 722 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at the c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  Furthermore, a reversible capacity of ∼480 mAh g-1 was obtained at much higher c.d. of 5 A g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 5-Sn/C was attributed to the effective combination of ultrasmall Sn nanoparticles, uniform distribution, and porous carbon network structure, which simultaneously solved the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact, and particle aggregation facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrEUpsr6zyRM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhrkvgEYmBzDA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFSqtrnI&amp;md5=16375b393bb7b49cb6ff0d1e9b5bac6c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1088/1361-6528/aa6329"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yazdani, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kashfi-Sadabad, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palmieri, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mustain, W.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Green and Facile Fabrication of Hollow Porous MnO/C Microspheres from Microalgaes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xia, Yang; Xiao, Zhen; Dou, Xiao; Huang, Hui; Lu, Xianghong; Yan, Rongjun; Gan, Yongping; Zhu, Wenjun; Tu, Jiangping; Zhang, Wenkui; Tao, Xinyong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7083-7092</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow porous micro/nanostructures with high surface area and shell permeability have attracted tremendous attention.  Particularly, the synthesis and structural tailoring of diverse hollow porous materials is regarded as a crucial step toward the realization of high-performance electrode materials, which has several advantages including a large contact area with electrolyte, a superior structural stability, and a short transport path for Li+ ions.  Meanwhile, owing to the inexpensive, abundant, environmentally benign, and renewable biol. resources provided by nature, great efforts have been devoted to understand and practice the biotemplating technol., which was considered as an effective strategy to achieve morphol.-controllable materials with structural specialty, complexity, and related unique properties.  Herein, the authors are inspired by the natural microalgae with its special features (easy availability, biol. activity, and C sources) to develop a green and facile biotemplating method to fabricate monodisperse MnO/C microspheres for Li-ion batteries.  Due to the unique hollow porous structure in which MnO nanoparticles were tightly embedded into a porous C matrix and form a penetrative shell, MnO/C microspheres exhibited high reversible specific capacity of 700 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, excellent cycling stability with 94% capacity retention, and enhanced rate performance of 230 mA-h g-1 at 3 A g-1.  This green, sustainable, and economical strategy will extend the scope of biotemplating synthesis for exploring other functional materials in various structure-dependent applications such as catalysis, gas sensing, and energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsQKzF09PBdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhrkvgEYmBzDA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOqurfM&amp;md5=592dcca56bd411456287f5b12b2386e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201608489"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, Y.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Goodenough, J.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of Nitrogen-Doped MnO/Graphene Nanosheets Hybrid Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kejun; Han, Pengxian; Gu, Lin; Zhang, Lixue; Liu, Zhihong; Kong, Qingshan; Zhang, Chuanjian; Dong, Shanmu; Zhang, Zhongyi; Yao, Jianhua; Xu, Hongxia; Cui, Guanglei; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped MnO/graphene nanosheets (N-MnO/GNS) hybrid material was synthesized by a simple hydrothermal method followed by NH3 annealing.  The samples were studied by XRD, Raman spectroscopy, XPS, TEM and AFM.  N-doped MnO (N-MnO) nanoparticles were homogeneously anchored on the thin layers of N-doped GNS (N-GNS) to form an efficient electronic/ionic mixed conducting network.  This nanostructured hybrid exhibited a reversible electrochem. Li storage capacity ≤772 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g after 90 cycles, and an excellent rate capability of 202 mA-h/g at a high c.d. of 5 A/g.  N-MnO/GNS hybrid is a candidate high capacity anode material for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrUSYTQEMzwbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhrkvgEYmBzDA"> &gt;&gt;                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b00942"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MnFe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">16</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3321</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3328</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b00942</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D3321-3328%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BYu%26author%3DL.%2BJiao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DMnFe2O4%2540C%2BNanofibers%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b09559&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MnFe2O4@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Yu, Chuanming; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3321-3328</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnFe2O4 nanodots (∼3.3 nm) homogeneously dispersed in porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (denoted as MFO@C) were prepd. by a feasible electrospinning technique.  Meanwhile, MFO@C with the character of flexible free-standing membrane was directly used as binder- and current collector-free anode for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting high electrochem. performance with high-rate capability (305 mA h g-1 at 10000 mA g-1 in comparison of 504 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1) and ultralong cycling life (ca. 90% capacity retention after 4200 cycles).  The Na-storage mechanism was systematically studied, revealing that MnFe2O4 is converted into metallic Mn and Fe after the first discharge (MnFe2O4 + 8Na+ + 8e- → Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O) and then to MnO and Fe2O3 during the following charge (Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O → MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e-).  The subsequent cycles occur through reversible redox reactions of MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e- &lt;-&gt; Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O, of which the redn./oxidn. of MnO/Mn takes place at a lower potential than that of Fe2O3/Fe.  Furthermore, a soft package sodium-ion full battery with MFO@C anode and Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode was assembled, delivering a stable capacity of ∼400 mA h g-1 for MFO@C (with 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and a promising energy d. of 77.8 Wh kg-1 for the whole battery.  This is owing to the distinctive structure of very-fine MnFe2O4 nanodots embedded in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers, which effectively improves the utilization rate of active materials, facilitates the transportation of electrons and Na+ ions, and prevents the particle pulverization/agglomeration upon prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_fovS2KMexbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgExqNyZme7pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XlsFKqtLk%253D&amp;md5=1f0fa2211d961158137c8cc4eb8fdd4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Henderson, W. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard Carbon Nanoparticles as High-Capacity, High-Stability Anodic Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">19</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">279</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">288</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D19%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D279-288%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DL.%2BXiao%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26author%3DW.%2BA.%2BHenderson%26author%3DM.%2BL.%2BSushko%26author%3DY.%2BShao%26author%3DJ.%2BXiao%26author%3DW.%2BWang%26author%3DM.%2BH.%2BEngelhard%26author%3DZ.%2BNie%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26title%3DHard%2BCarbon%2BNanoparticles%2Bas%2BHigh-Capacity%252C%2BHigh-Stability%2BAnodic%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2015.10.034&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b09559&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2015.10.034&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon nanoparticles as high-capacity, high-stability anodic materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Lifen; Cao, Yuliang; Henderson, Wesley A.; Sushko, Maria L.; Shao, Yuyan; Xiao, Jie; Wang, Wei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Nie, Zimin; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">279-288</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon nanoparticles (HCNP) were synthesized by the pyrolysis of a polyaniline precursor.  The measured Na+ cation diffusion coeff. (10-13-10-15 cm2 s-1) in the HCNP obtained at 1150 °C is two orders of magnitude lower than that of Li+ in graphite (10-10-10-13 cm2 s-1), indicating that reducing the carbon particle size is very important for improving electrochem. performance.  These measurements also enable a clear visualization of the stepwise reaction phases and rate changes which occur throughout the insertion/extn. processes in HCNP, The electrochem. measurements also show that the nano-sized HCNP obtained at 1150 °C exhibited higher practical capacity at voltages lower than 1.2 V (vs. Na/Na+), as well as a prolonged cycling stability, which is attributed to an optimum spacing of 0.366 nm between the graphitic layers and the nano particular size resulting in a low-barrier Na+ cation insertion.  These results suggest that HCNP is a very promising high-capacity/stability anode for low cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0215ZE-6YJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgExqNyZme7pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVaqtrrE&amp;md5=93cb764059ea5aaa3841222611c03416</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00744B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controllable Synthesis of Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Nanodots@Nitrogen-Doped Graphene and its Application for High Energy Density Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.     <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5523-5531</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Supercapacitors using ionic liqs. (ILs) as electrolytes have triggered great interest due to their much higher energy d. when compared to aq. supercapacitors.  Although Mn oxides have obvious capacitive contribution in ILs and thus can be used as electrode materials for IL-based supercapacitors, they suffer from low specific capacitance in ILs.  Here, Mn3O4 nanodots loaded on N-doped graphene sheets (denoted as Mn3O4 NDs@NG) are prepd. through a facile 1-pot solvothermal method with the presence of octylamine as the surfactant.  Octylamine plays an important role in obtaining quantum-sized Mn3O4 NDs and controlling their dispersion degree on the surface of NG.  With an optimal loading mass of Mn3O4 NDs, the corresponding Mn3O4 NDs@NG material is able to achieve a high specific capacitance of 158.9 F/g in a given IL and shows excellent rate capability.  On this basis, a sym. supercapacitor is assembled based on such a Mn3O4 NDs@NG, which delivers a high energy d. of 90.7 Wh/Kg in the IL electrolyte.  An asym. supercapacitor is also built using such a Mn3O4 NDs@NG and activated C as the neg. and pos. electrode, resp.  This asym. device shows a higher energy d. of 124.4 Wh/Kg compared to the sym. one, and it still can deliver 55.8 Wh/Kg at a large power d. of 29.9 KW/Kg.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpO5FCFs3o5MrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgExqNyZme7pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXis1WktL0%253D&amp;md5=50268d34f4d3e6e310ebc6d06140560c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201601959"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bu, X.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Size-Tunable Olive-Like Anatase TiO2 Coated with Carbon as Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Jun; Zhang, Yan; Zou, Guoqiang; Huang, Zhaodong; Li, Simin; Liao, Hanxiao; Wang, Jufeng; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5554-5563</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Olive-shaped anatase TiO2 with tunable sizes in nanoscale are designed employing polyvinyl alc. (PVA) as structure directing agents to impact on structure shaping and size manipulation.  Notably, the introduced PVA simultaneously serves as C sources, bringing about a homogeneous C layer with intimate coupling interfaces for boosted electronic cond.  Constructed from tiny cryst. grains, the uniformly dispersed C-coated TiO2 nano-olives (TOC) possess subtle loose structure internally for prompt Na+ transportation.  When used for Na-ion storage, the size effects are increasingly significant at high charge-discharge rates, leading to the much superior rate performances of TOC with the smallest size.  Bestowed by the improved Na+ adsorption and diffusion kinetics together with the promoted electron transfer, it delivers a high specific capacity of 267 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C (33.6 mA g-1) and sustains 110 mA h g-1 at a rather high rate of 20 C.  Even after cycled at 10 C over 1000 cycles, a considerable capacity of 125 mA h g-1 with a retention of 94.6% is still obtained, highlighting its long-term cyclability and high-rate capabilities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsTZm-u-NF0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgExqNyZme7pQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVChtbzF&amp;md5=f143b6730d4e33771e789c43b778393f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1039/C7CC00087A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MnOOH Nanorods as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                 10.1039/C7CC00087A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D53%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D2435-2438%26journal%3DChem.%2BCommun.%26author%3DL.%2BShao%26author%3DQ.%2BZhao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DMnOOH%2BNanorods%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7CC00087A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b09559&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7CC00087A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MnOOH nanorods as high-performance anodes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Lianyi; Zhao, Qing; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2435-2438</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHCOFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-7345</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnOOH nanorods, which were prepd. using a hydrothermal method, have been used for the first time as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  The as-prepd. MnOOH nanorods with lengths of 1.2-3.7 μm and diams. of 60-90 nm delivered high performance of reversible electrochem. Na/Na+ storage such as an initial discharge capacity of 485.5 mA h g-1 at 80 mA g-1, a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 86.7% and a low av. potential polarization of 0.36 V.  Instrumental analyses with ex situ XRD, TEM and XPS show that the sodium storage mechanism in MnOOH can be related to the reversible formation of MnO and NaOH.  This work demonstrates that cheap MnOOH nanorods are potential anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0RnhEy9Fg6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lipuWSTqYpZTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvF2hur8%253D&amp;md5=336562e3da2cc591a2a5bc20b4cc014e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201603716"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Ribbon Assembled Core-Sheath MnO@Graphene Scrolls as Hierarchically Ordered 3D Porous Electrodes for Fast and Durable Lithium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">26</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">7754</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">7765</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201603716</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D26%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D7754-7765%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DP.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BGao%26author%3DB.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BWu%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BDou%26title%3DNitrogen-Doped%2BGraphene%2BRibbon%2BAssembled%2BCore-Sheath%2BMnO%2540Graphene%2BScrolls%2Bas%2BHierarchically%2BOrdered%2B3D%2BPorous%2BElectrodes%2Bfor%2BFast%2Band%2BDurable%2BLithium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201603716&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b09559&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201603716&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Ribbon Assembled Core-Sheath MnO@Graphene Scrolls as Hierarchically Ordered 3D Porous Electrodes for Fast and Durable Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yun; Chen, Penghui; Gao, Xu; Wang, Bo; Liu, Heng; Wu, Hao; Liu, Huakun; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7754-7765</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene scroll is an emerging 1D tubular form of graphitic carbon that has potential applications in electrochem. energy storage.  However, it still remains a challenge to composite graphene scrolls with other nanomaterials for building advanced electrode configuration with fast and durable lithium storage properties.  Here, a transition-metal-oxide-based hierarchically ordered 3D porous electrode is designed based on assembling 1D core-sheath MnO@N-doped graphene scrolls with 2D N-doped graphene ribbons.  In the resulting architecture, porous MnO nanowires confined in tubular graphene scrolls are mech. isolated but electronically well-connected, while the interwoven graphene ribbons offer continuous conductive paths for electron transfer in all directions.  Moreover, the elastic graphene scrolls together with enough internal voids are able to accommodate the vol. expansion of the enclosed MnO.  Because of these merits, the as-built electrode manifests ultrahigh rate capability (349 mAh g-1 at 8.0 A g-1; 205 mAh g-1 at 15.0 A g-1) and robust cycling stability (812 mAh g-1 remaining after 1000 cycles at 2.0 A g-1) and is the most efficient MnO-based anode ever reported for lithium-ion batteries.  This unique multidimensional and hierarchically ordered structure design is believed to hold great potential in generalizable synthesis of graphene scrolls composited with oxide nanowires for mutifuctional energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh8xcBh8-tE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lipuWSTqYpZTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFenu7%252FM&amp;md5=632f9f9db962b375bfe78764a2077cd9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1016/S0378-7753(99)00180-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Takeda, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Imanishi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ichikawa, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamamoto, O.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Study of the Cycling Performance of Finely Dispersed Lithium Alloy Composite Electrodes under High Li-Utilization</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Organic Framework Derived Porous Hollow Co3O4/N-C Polyhedron Composite with Excellent Energy Storage Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Wenpei; Zhang, Yu; Fan, Lili; Zhang, Liangliang; Dai, Fangna; Wang, Rongming; Sun, Daofeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10602-10609</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) derived transition metal oxides exhibit enhanced performance in energy conversion and storage.  In this work, porous hollow Co3O4 with N-doped carbon coating (Co3O4/N-C) polyhedrons have been prepd. using cobalt-based MOFs as a sacrificial template.  Assembled from tiny nanoparticles and N-doped carbon coating, Co3O4/N-C composite shortens the diffusion length of Li+/Na+ ions and possesses an enhanced cond.  The porous and hollow structure is also beneficial for tolerating vol. changes in the galvanostatic discharge/charge cycles as lithium/sodium battery anode materials.  As a result, it can exhibit impressive cycling and rating performance.  At 1000 mA g-1, the specific capacities maintained stable values of ∼620 mAh g-1 within 2000 cycles as anodes in lithium ion battery, while the specific capacity keeps at 229 mAh g-1 within 150 cycles as sodium ion battery anode.  The work shows comparable cycling performance in lithium ion battery but even better high-rate cycling stability as sodium ion battery anode.  Herein, a facile method is provided to construct high electrochem. performance oxide/N-C composite electrode using new MOFs as sacrificial template.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohdLj6rKhXM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lipuWSTqYpZTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktV2lurc%253D&amp;md5=59b9e06ccf54aa8f4145800d531cb607</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref62'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b05041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zou, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bhaway, S. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal Organic Frameworks Derived Hierarchical Hollow NiO/Ni/Graphene Composites for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">10</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">377</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">386</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal Organic Frameworks Derived Hierarchical Hollow NiO/Ni/Graphene Composites for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Feng; Chen, Yu-Ming; Liu, Kewei; Yu, Zitian; Liang, Wenfeng; Bhaway, Sarang M.; Gao, Min; Zhu, Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">377-386</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ni-based metal org. frameworks (Ni-MOFs) with unique hierarchical hollow ball-in-ball nanostructure were synthesized by solvothermal reactions.  After successive carbonization and oxidn. treatments, hierarchical NiO/Ni nanocrystals covered with a graphene shell were obtained with the hollow ball-in-ball nanostructure intact.  The resulting materials exhibited superior performance as the anode in lithium ion batteries (LIBs): they provide high reversible specific capacity (1144 mAh/g), excellent cyclability (nearly no capacity loss after 1000 cycles) and rate performance (805 mAh/g at 15 A/g).  In addn., the hierarchical NiO/Ni/Graphene composites demonstrated promising performance as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Such a superior lithium and sodium storage performance is derived from the well-designed hierarchical hollow ball-in-ball structure of NiO/Ni/Graphene composites, which not only mitigates the vol. expansion of NiO during the cycles but also provides a continuous highly conductive graphene matrix to facilitate the fast charge transfer and form a stable SEI layer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFsltJ-ZhbyLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lipuWSTqYpZTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFSmtbzM&amp;md5=98be0e8818487e6970ee353c03aa159e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref63'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b11238"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospinning Synthesis of Mesoporous MnCoNiO<sub>x</sub>@Double-Carbon Nanofibers for Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes with Pseudocapacitive Behavior and Long Cycle Life</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The design of sodium ion batteries is proposed based on the use of flexible membrane composed of ultrasmall transition metal oxides.  In this paper, the prepn. of CuO quantum dots (≈2 nm) delicately embedded in carbon nanofibers (denoted as 2-CuO@C) with a thin film via a feasible electrospinning method is reported.  The CuO content can be controlled by altering the synthetic conditions and is optimized to 54 wt%.  As binder-free anode for sodium ion batteries, 2-CuO@C delivers an initial reversible capacity of 528 mA h/g at the c.d. of 100 mA/g, an exceptional rate capability of 250 mA h/g at 5000 mA/g, and an ultra-stable capacity of 401 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 500 mA/g.  The enhancement of electrochem. performance is attributed to the unique structure of 2-CuO@C, which offers a variety of advantages: highly conductive carbon matrix suppressing agglomeration of CuO grains, interconnected nanofibers ensuring short transport length for electrons, well-dispersed CuO quantum dots leading to highly utilization rate, and good mech. properties resulting in strong electrode integrity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoogoQcQ6j0ZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO71tzlULHcw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVKgu7vP&amp;md5=bc4abeee5df0a98f8d12865d883b654b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref65"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref65'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">65</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit65" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA00236F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Superior Sodium-Ion Storage Performance of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>@Nitrogen-Doped Carbon: Derived from a Metal-Organic Framework</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5428</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5435</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
