                        cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior sodium-ion storage performance of Co3O4@nitrogen-doped carbon: derived from a metal-organic framework</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Ying; Wang, Caiyun; Wang, Yijing; Liu, Huakun; Huang, Zhenguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5428-5435</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped C coated Co3O4 nanoparticles (Co3O4@NC) with high Na-ion storage capacity and unprecedented long-life cycling stability are reported.  The Co3O4@NC was derived from a metal-org. framework ZIF-67, where the Co ions and org. linkers were, resp., converted to Co3O4 nanoparticle cores and N-doped C shells through a controlled 2-step annealing process.  The Co3O4@NC shows a porous nature with a surface area of 101 m2 g-1.  When applied as an anode for Na ion batteries (SIBs), Co3O4@NC delivers a high reversible capacity of 506, 317, and 263 mA h g-1 at 100, 400, and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  A capacity degrdn. of 0.03% per cycle over 1100 cycles was achieved at a high c.d. of 1000 mA g-1.  The outstanding Na-ion storage performance can be ascribed to the N-doped C coating (NC), which facilitates the capacitive reaction, minimizes the vol. changes of Co3O4, and also enhances the electronic cond.  This work sheds light on how to develop high-performance metal oxide@NC nanocomposites for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9srwVE0kC6bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO71tzlULHcw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslWjtLg%253D&amp;md5=36f8823fd3051b22c5e45e40e63400bc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref66"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref66'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">66</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit66" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b09444"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/Graphene Composite Nanosheets with Enhanced Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">30899</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">30907</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit66R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">66</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous Fe2O3/Graphene Composite Nanosheets with Enhanced Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Dan; Zhou, Jisheng; Chen, Xiaohong; Song, Huaihe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">30899-30907</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the increasing use of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), developing cost-effective anode materials, such as metal oxide, for Na-ion storage is one of the most attractive topics.  Due to the obviously larger ion radius of Na than that of Li, most metal oxide electrode materials fail to exhibit the same high performance for SIBs like that of Li-ion batteries.  Herein, iron oxide was employed to demonstrate a concept that rationally designing an amorphous structure should be useful to enhance Na-ion storage performance of a metal oxide.  Amorphous Fe2O3/graphene composite nanosheets (Fe2O3@GNS) were successfully synthesized by a facile approach as anodes for SIBs.  It reveals that amorphous Fe2O3 nanoparticles with an av. diam. of 5 nm were uniformly anchored on the surface of graphene nanosheets by the strong C-O-Fe oxygen-bridge bond.  Compared to well-cryst. Fe2O3, amorphous Fe2O3@GNS exhibited superior sodium storage properties such as high electrochem. activity, high initial Coulombic efficiency of 81.2%, and good rate performance.  At a c.d. of 100 mA/g, amorphous Fe2O3@GNS composites show a specific capacity of 440 mAh/g, which is obviously higher than the specific capacity of 284 mAh/g of cryst. Fe2O3.  Even at a high c.d. of 2 A/g, amorphous Fe2O3@GNS composites still exhibit a specific capacity as high as 219 mAh/g.  The excellent electrochem. performance should be attributed to the amorphous structures of Fe2O3 as well as strongly interfacial interaction between Fe2O3 and GNS, which not only accommodate more electrochem. active sites and provide the more transmission channels for sodium ions but also benefit electron transfer as well as effectively buffer the vol. change of host materials during sodiation and desodiation.  This concept for designing amorphous iron oxide anodes for SIBs is also expected to facilitate prepn. of various amorphous nanostructure of other metal oxides and improve their Na-ion storage performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo7MVJUARTAx7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO71tzlULHcw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslCktLvN&amp;md5=8a895886e1ae787a072abe496e1f95cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref67"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref67'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">67</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit67" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b09496"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D-0D Graphene-Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Quantum Dot Hybrids as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater.                 10.1021/acsami.6b09496</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D26878-26885%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BJia%26author%3DQ.%2BZhu%26author%3DB.%2BCao%26author%3DR.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DB.%2BXu%26title%3D3D-0D%2BGraphene-Fe3O4%2BQuantum%2BDot%2BHybrids%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.6b09496&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b09559&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.6b09496&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit67R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">67</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D-0D Graphene-Fe3O4 Quantum Dot Hybrids as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Zhu, Qizhen; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Wang, Yu; Wu, Feng; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">26878-26885</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides can be considered as appealing candidates for sodium ion battery anode materials because these low-cost materials possess high capacity and enhanced safety.  However, the practical application of these materials is usually limited by their low electronic cond. and serious vol. change during the charging-discharging process.  Herein, we report the fabrication of 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids by a facile one-pot hydrothermal approach as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Fe3O4 quantum dots with an av. size of 4.9 nm are anchored on the surface of 3D structured graphene nanosheets homogeneously.  Such unique hierarchical structure are advantageous for enlarging the electrode/electrolyte interface area and enhancing the electrochem. activity of the hybrid materials, inhibiting particle aggregation of Fe3O4 and accommodating their vol. change during the charging-discharging process as well as enabling fast diffusion of electrons and rapid transfer of electrolyte ions.  Consequently, the 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids exhibit ultrahigh sodium storage capacity (525 mAh/g at 30 mA/g), outstanding cycling stability (312 mAh/g after 200 cycles at 50 mA/g) and superior rate performance (56 mAh/g at 10 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqySiZNElc5Z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhO71tzlULHcw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFanu7rN&amp;md5=18e241446b270b8baeccc2c7fb9c0f0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref68"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref68'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">68</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit68" data-doi="10.1039/C6CC07346H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dong, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ci, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Metal-Organic Framework-Derived Graphene@Nitrogen Doped Carbon@Ultrafine TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanocomposites as High Rate and Long-Life Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit68R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">68</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic framework-derived graphene@nitrogen doped carbon@ultrafine TiO2 nanocomposites as high rate and long-life anodes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zhen; An, Yongling; Xu, Xiaoyan; Dong, Chenglong; Feng, Jinkui; Ci, Lijie; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>

                        rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liSwGNsPbzajA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201601621"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Foster, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, CDs (C dots), for the 1st time, are proposed as designer additives for graphene-rich petal-like rutile TiO2 (termed: G/P-RTiO2).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we report a simple but effective method to fill carbon nanotube (CNT) channels with a dense distribution of Fe3O4 nanoparticles, to produce Fe3O4@CNT.  The resulting novel heterogeneous nanostructure displayed multiple attractive features as an anode material in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, this nanostructure displayed voids that apparently effectively prevented active material from aggregating and helped to accommodate their volumetric expansion during the cycling process.  In addn., most solid electrolyte interphases (SEIs) formed on the surfaces of the CNT shells instead of on individual Fe3O4 nanoparticles, limiting the amt. of SEIs and increasing the stability of the Fe3O4 nanoparticles.  As a result, when tested for LIBs, the Fe3O4@CNT nanocomposite exhibited an excellent rate capacity and cycling performance in half and full cells.  A high reversible capacity of 720 mA h g-1 was obtained after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1, and when the c.d. was increased to 8 A g-1, the specific capacity was 400 mA h g-1.  As for SIBs, a specific capacity of 377 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 was achieved after 300 cycles.  The facile synthetic route and unique nanostructure design may be extended to high-performance anode materials for LIBs and SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPJRClqmvTG7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7vbAukYU2ng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslGgsbrK&amp;md5=e63c2974a1c64aa5ee40bb0393e20173</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1039/C5CC01152C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kuo, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of active water oxidn. catalysts is crit. to achieve high efficiency in overall water splitting.  Recently, sub-10-nm-sized monodispersed partially-oxidized manganese oxide nanoparticles were shown to exhibit not only superior catalytic performance for oxygen evolution, but also unique electrokinetics, compared to their bulk counterparts.  In the present work, the water-oxidizing mechanism of partially-oxidized MnO nanoparticles was investigated using integrated in-situ spectroscopic and electrokinetic analyses.  It is successfully demonstrated that, in contrast to previously reported manganese (Mn)-based catalysts, Mn(III) species are stably generated on the surface of MnO nanoparticles via a proton-coupled electron transfer pathway.  Furthermore, it is confirmed as to MnO nanoparticles that the one-electron oxidn. step from Mn(II) to Mn(III) is no longer the rate detg. step for water oxidn. and that Mn(IV)=O species are generated as reaction intermediates during catalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJVa_16A1817Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7vbAukYU2ng"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGqsr3M&amp;md5=ab5dda6dfc053547eac804f331eba5f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA08330G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, M.-Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible High-Energy Asymmetric Supercapacitors Based on MnO@C Composite Nanosheet Electrodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing asym. supercapacitors (ASCs) is a promising alternative to achieve both wide voltage windows and high energy densities to meet the application requirements of hybrid vehicles and renewable energy systems.  However, a major limitation of high performance asym. supercapacitors lies in neg. electrode materials which possess relatively low specific capacitance compared to pos. electrode materials.  Herein, a novel MnO@C composite nanosheet array directly grown on conductive carbon cloth as a neg. electrode is prepd. successfully, which exhibits a large specific capacitance of 662.9 F g-1 at a c.d. of 3.7 A g-1 and an areal capacitance of 716 mF cm-2 at a c.d. of 4 mA cm-2.  Afterward, a flexible ASC is successfully assembled with Co3O4 nanosheets and MnO@C nanosheets as the pos. electrode and neg. electrode, resp.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries have attained great success in commercialization owing to their high energy d.  However, the relatively delaying discharge/charge severely hinders their high power applications due to intrinsically diffusion-controlled lithium storage of the electrode.  This study demonstrates an ever-increasing surface redox capacitive lithium storage originating from an unique microstructure evolution during cycling in a novel RGO-MnO-RGO sandwich nanostructure.  Such surface pseudocapacitance is dynamically in equil. with diffusion-controlled lithium storage, thereby achieving an unprecedented rate capability (331.9 mAh/g at 40 A/g, 379 mAh/g after 4000 cycles at 15 A/g) with outstanding cycle stability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To tackle the issue of inferior cycle stability and rate capability for MnO anode materials in lithium ion batteries, a facile strategy is explored to prep. a hybrid material consisting of MnO nanocrystals grown on conductive graphene nanosheets.  The prepd. MnO/graphene hybrid anode exhibits a reversible capacity as high as 2014.1 mAh g-1 after 150 discharge/charge cycles at 200 mA g-1, excellent rate capability (625.8 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1), and superior cyclability (843.3 mAh g-1 even after 400 discharge/charge cycles at 2000 mA g-1 with only 0.01% capacity loss per cycle).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous hybrid materials with designed micro/nano-sub-structures have been recognized as promising anodes for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their high capacity and reliable performance.  The low elec. cond. and side-reactions at the interface of electrode/electrolyte prohibit their practical applications.  Carbon material modification can effectively enhance the cond. and mech. properties, and suppress the direct contact between the electrode and electrolyte, leading to enhanced performance.  Herein, unique porous MnO with micro/nano-architectures has been in situ decorated with carbon layers on the surface and by carbon nanotube doping between the particles (denoted as MnO@C/CNTs) by a catalytic chem. vapor deposition (CCVD) treatment.  As anodes in LIBs, these MnO@C/CNTs exhibit remarkable cycling performance (1266 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and good rate capability (850 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1).  The inspiring performance is assocd. with the carbon modified porous micro/nano-structure features which can buffer the vol. expansion and promote the ion/electron transfer at the interface of electrode/electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpK1Oxo39q8WrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3FkBwG4efDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFOqtrbF&amp;md5=97c52c68651b2c7cec918b1f7d9a7c6b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201605820"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Confined Amorphous Red Phosphorus in MOF-Derived N-Doped Microporous Carbon as a Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A B-doped C layer (BC) was coated on porous micron-sized Li4Ti5O12 (LTO) via a facile wet-chem. method for use as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries.  As detd. by x-ray photoemission spectroscopy and Raman spectroscopy, 3 different species (BC3, BC2O, and BCO2) were doped in the C layer on the surface of LTO.  These heteroatoms lead to abundant extrinsic defects in the C layer that result in improved Na-ion diffusivity across the active material.  Using electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, the diffusion coeff. of the B-doped C-coated LTO (BC-LTO) is 2.241 × 10-15 cm2 s-1.  The BC-LTO exhibited 85% and 60% higher Na-ion diffusivity than pristine LTO and C-coated LTO (C-LTO), resp.  Also, electron-deficient B in BC3 enhances the elec. cond. through pos. charged holes that carry electrons through the C structure.  Accordingly, the BC-LTO electrode showed a high specific capacity of 148 mA-h g-1 at 0.5 C and 98.4 mA-h g-1 at 10C rate.  The BC-LTO anode demonstrated a great capacity retention of ∼90% at 1 and 10C after 300 cycles.  These findings demonstrate the promising potential of LTO as a high-performance anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgDus9NKdbdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh3FkBwG4efDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFCgt73F&amp;md5=242e1f1fc5d3bb47237faa2b2f76e571</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201104634"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Noble metal nanoparticles (MNPs) have attracted continuous attention due to their promising applications in chem., physics, bioscience, medicine and materials science.  As an alternative to conventional soln. chem. routes, MNPs can be directly synthesized through a conjugated polymer (CP) mediated technique utilizing the redox chem. of CPs to chem. reduce the metal ions and modulate the size, morphol., and structure of the MNPs.  The as-prepd. multifunctional CP-MNP nanocomposites have shown application potentials as highly sensitive surface enhanced Raman spectroscopy (SERS) substrates, effective heterogeneous catalysts for org. synthesis and electrochem., and key components for electronic and sensing devices.  In this tutorial review, we begin with a brief introduction to the chem. nature and redox properties of CPs that enable the spontaneous redn. of noble metal ions to form MNPs.  We then focus on recent progress in control over the size, morphol. and structure of MNPs during the conjugated polymer mediated syntheses of CP-MNP nanocomposites.  Finally, we highlight the multifunctional CP-MNP nanocomposites toward their applications in sensing, catalysis, and electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8wtExX8CyjLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lggq31uHAnCTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFWhsL4%253D&amp;md5=20e27af37db3db6c6b0b766ef3706f3f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.3390/polym8100366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Du, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heteroatom-Doped Carbon Nanostructures Derived from Conjugated Polymers for Energy Applications</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Polymers</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">366</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doped carbon materials have been one of the most remarkable families of materials with promising applications in fuel cells, supercapacitors, and batteries.  Among them, conjugated polymer (CP)-derived heteroatom-doped carbon materials exhibit remarkable electrochem. performances because the heteroatoms can be preserved at a relatively high content and keep stable under harsh working conditions.  In this review, we summarized recent advances in the rational design and various applications of CP-derived heteroatom-doped carbon materials, including polyaniline (PANI), polypyrrole (PPy), and their ramification-derived carbons, as well as transition metal-carbon nanocomposites.  The key point of considering CP-derived heteroatom-doped carbon materials as important candidates of electrode materials is that CPs contain only nonmetallic elements and some key heteroatoms in their backbones which provide great chances for the synthesis of metal-free heteroatom-doped carbon nanostructures.  The presented examples in this review will provide new insights in designing and optimizing heteroatom-doped carbon materials for the development of anode and cathode materials for electrochem. device applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonB3tEb8RIerVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lggq31uHAnCTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktlajurc%253D&amp;md5=ae545e13ffccccc410d917cff8a72892</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1021/ja402450a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Silva, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Voiry, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chhowalla, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Asefa, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Metal-Free Electrocatalysts for Oxygen Reduction: Polyaniline-Derived N- and O-doped Mesoporous Carbons</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient metal-free electrocatalysts for oxygen reduction: polyaniline-derived N- and O-doped mesoporous carbons</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Silva, Rafael; Voiry, Damien; Chhowalla, Manish; Asefa, Tewodros</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The oxygen redn. reaction (ORR)-one of the two half-reactions in fuel cells-is one of the bottlenecks that has prevented fuel cells from finding a wide range of applications today.  This is because ORR is inherently a sluggish reaction; it is also because inexpensive and sustainable ORR electrocatalysts that are not only efficient but also are based on earth-abundant elements are hard to come by.  Herein we report the synthesis of novel carbon-based materials that can contribute to solving these challenges assocd. with ORR.  Mesoporous oxygen- and nitrogen-doped carbons were synthesized from in situ polymd. mesoporous silica-supported polyaniline (PANI) by carbonization of the latter, followed by etching away the mesoporous silica template from it.  The synthetic method also allowed the immobilization of different metals such as Fe and Co easily into the system.  While all the resulting materials showed outstanding electrocatalytic activity toward ORR, the metal-free, PANI-derived mesoporous carbon (dubbed PDMC), in particular, exhibited the highest activity, challenging conventional paradigms.  This unprecedented activity by the metal-free PDMC toward ORR was attributed to the synergetic activities of nitrogen and oxygen (or hydroxyl) species that were implanted in it by PANI/mesoporous silica during pyrolysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqu_zhHIpLhBrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lggq31uHAnCTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXntVOkurw%253D&amp;md5=f05c2e7c88034ee0359818cc8846c53b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.5b00292"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ding, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nie, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qi, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Shape Fixing via Salt Recrystallization: A Morphology-Controlled Approach To Convert Nanostructured Polymer to Carbon Nanomaterial as a Highly Active Catalyst for Oxygen Reduction Reaction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, the authors report a shape fixing via salt recrystn. method to efficiently synthesize N-doped C material with a large no. of active sites exposed to the 3-phase zones, for use as an ORR catalyst.  Self-assembled polyaniline with a 3-dimensional network structure was fixed and fully sealed inside NaCl via recrystn. of NaCl soln.  During pyrolysis, the NaCl crystal functions as a fully sealed nanoreactor, which facilitates N incorporation and graphitization. Use of the invented cathode catalyst in a p exchange membrane fuel cell produces a peak power of 600 mW cm-2, making this among the best nonprecious metal catalysts for the ORR reported so far.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped carbon was found to exhibit excellent activity as an electrocatalyst in renewable energy devices.  A controllable method to synthesize N-doped hierarchically porous carbons (PNCEs) partly with graphene-like structure using polyaniline (PANI)-polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP) composite as a carbon source via a soft-template process was reported.  The catalytic mechanism was thoroughly studied to better understand the relationship between the structure, Fe species and catalytic activity.  The PNCE prepd. at 1000°C displays the best performance achieving a max. power d. of 456 mW/cm2 and oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) onset potential of 0.90 V.  More prominently, the catalyst presents superior stability, as well as poison tolerance including methanol and SO2 to the com. JM-Pt/C catalyst in 0.5 M H2SO4.  The PVP is proven to tailor the structure, improve the surface area, and alter the transition metal species.  The PNCEs synthesized under NH3 exhibit considerably better catalytic activity toward ORR compared with the undoped carbon and PNCEs synthesized under an N2 atmosphere.  Furthermore, we find that the nitrogen bonding configurations, textural structure, Fe species and surface areas of PNCEs play key roles in the electrocatalytic activity towards the ORR.  The formed FeN4 species hosted in the micropores acts as the active component for ORR activity in PNCEs, although it is not the only contributor to the high performance of PNCEs.  The catalyst is expected to be a promising non-noble electrocatalyst for use in polymer electrolyte membrane fuel cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrdGZbXDYNSQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_y5Gguw0whw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlOjsbjM&amp;md5=9e9d9f5cf9573fca03733f0ed560f927</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Encapsulated in Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanofibers as a Free-Standing Anode for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small Sn nanodots (1-2 nm) were delicately encapsulated in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers through electrospinning and thermal treatment.  The size and content of Sn particles can be controlled by changing reaction conditions.  When evaluated as binder- and current collector-free anodes for rechargeable Na-ion batteries, Sn NDs@PNC nanofibers delivered a reversible capacity of 633 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More impressively, a capacity of 450 mA h g-1 even at 10 000 mA g-1 and 483 mA h g-1 over 1300 cycles at 2000 mA g-1 were achieved.  To our knowledge, this is the highest rate performance and cyclic stability of tin for Na storage.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of Sn NDs@PNC is attributed to the following: First, the ultra-small Sn NDs (1-2 nm) decreases the abs. strain and improve the utilization rate of active materials during sodiation/de-sodiation process; second, the uniform distribution of Sn NDs in the fibrous carbon matrix is an important factor to generate a balanced stress over the whole composite with maintaining the integrity of the electrode upon prolonged cycling; third, the 1D porous N-doped carbon frame can interlink into a 3D conductive network, which facilitates the electron and Na+ diffusion kinetics and buffers the large vol. fluctuation of Sn NDs and prevents their pulverization and aggregation.  Carbon fibers also serve as both current collector and conductive material - this avoids the common loss of electrochem. contact between the active materials and the current collector/conductive additives, and reduces the inactive wt. and vol. of cells thus improving the energy d.  This simple and scalable synthesis as well as the promising electrochem. performance encourages application of Sn-based materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnXAQ9MCRr0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_y5Gguw0whw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ks77J&amp;md5=c6f2a6fad6ab6e844a9149e974f0edf1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA04366B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ruan, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chou, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorus/N-Doped Carbon Nanofiber Composite as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been attracting intensive attention at present as the most promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries in large-scale elec. energy storage applications, due to the low-cost and natural abundance of sodium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is a very promising anode material for SIBs, with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  Recently, there have been many efforts devoted to phosphorus anode materials for SIBs.  As pure red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly, many attempts to prep. composite materials contg. phosphorus have been reported.  Here, we report the facile prepn. of a red phosphorus/N-doped carbon nanofiber composite (P/NCF) that can deliver a reversible capacity of 731 mA h g-1 in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), with a capacity retention of 57.3% over 55 cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The ability to deposit conformal catalytic thin films enables opportunities to achieve complex nanostructured designs for catalysis.  Atomic layer deposition (ALD) is capable of creating conformal thin films over complex substrates.  Here, ALD-MnOx on glassy C was studied as a catalyst for the O evolution reaction (OER) and the O redn. reaction (ORR), two reactions that are of growing interest due to their many applications in alternative energy technologies.  The films were characterized by XPS, x-ray diffraction, SEM, ellipsometry, and cyclic voltammetry.  The as-deposited films consist of Mn(II)O, which is a poor catalyst for the ORR, but highly active for the OER.  By controllably annealing the samples, Mn2O3 catalysts with good activity for both the ORR and OER were synthesized.  Hypotheses are presented to explain the large difference in the activity between the MnO and Mn2O3 catalysts for the ORR, but similar activity for the OER, including the effects of surface oxidn. under exptl. conditions.  These catalysts synthesized though ALD compare favorably to the best MnOx catalysts in the literature, demonstrating a viable way to produce highly active, conformal thin films from earth-abundant materials for the ORR and the OER.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCHku0Ms9RorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_y5Gguw0whw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFSmsLfO&amp;md5=77e61520524a8847d31c67b62c0e8eb9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201604108"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">S-Doped N-Rich Carbon Nanosheets with Expanded Interlayer Distance as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. The 5-Sn/C showed an initial discharge capacity of 1014 mAh g-1 and a capacity retention of 722 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at the c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  Furthermore, a reversible capacity of ∼480 mAh g-1 was obtained at much higher c.d. of 5 A g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 5-Sn/C was attributed to the effective combination of ultrasmall Sn nanoparticles, uniform distribution, and porous carbon network structure, which simultaneously solved the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact, and particle aggregation facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrEUpsr6zyRM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgv8FXad-lRVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFSqtrnI&amp;md5=16375b393bb7b49cb6ff0d1e9b5bac6c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1088/1361-6528/aa6329"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yazdani, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kashfi-Sadabad, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palmieri, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mustain, W.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7083-7092</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow porous micro/nanostructures with high surface area and shell permeability have attracted tremendous attention.  Particularly, the synthesis and structural tailoring of diverse hollow porous materials is regarded as a crucial step toward the realization of high-performance electrode materials, which has several advantages including a large contact area with electrolyte, a superior structural stability, and a short transport path for Li+ ions.  Meanwhile, owing to the inexpensive, abundant, environmentally benign, and renewable biol. resources provided by nature, great efforts have been devoted to understand and practice the biotemplating technol., which was considered as an effective strategy to achieve morphol.-controllable materials with structural specialty, complexity, and related unique properties.  Herein, the authors are inspired by the natural microalgae with its special features (easy availability, biol. activity, and C sources) to develop a green and facile biotemplating method to fabricate monodisperse MnO/C microspheres for Li-ion batteries.  Due to the unique hollow porous structure in which MnO nanoparticles were tightly embedded into a porous C matrix and form a penetrative shell, MnO/C microspheres exhibited high reversible specific capacity of 700 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, excellent cycling stability with 94% capacity retention, and enhanced rate performance of 230 mA-h g-1 at 3 A g-1.  This green, sustainable, and economical strategy will extend the scope of biotemplating synthesis for exploring other functional materials in various structure-dependent applications such as catalysis, gas sensing, and energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsQKzF09PBdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgv8FXad-lRVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOqurfM&amp;md5=592dcca56bd411456287f5b12b2386e6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201608489"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, Y.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Goodenough, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped MnO/graphene nanosheets (N-MnO/GNS) hybrid material was synthesized by a simple hydrothermal method followed by NH3 annealing.  The samples were studied by XRD, Raman spectroscopy, XPS, TEM and AFM.  N-doped MnO (N-MnO) nanoparticles were homogeneously anchored on the thin layers of N-doped GNS (N-GNS) to form an efficient electronic/ionic mixed conducting network.  This nanostructured hybrid exhibited a reversible electrochem. Li storage capacity ≤772 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g after 90 cycles, and an excellent rate capability of 202 mA-h/g at a high c.d. of 5 A/g.  N-MnO/GNS hybrid is a candidate high capacity anode material for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrUSYTQEMzwbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgT8AA11eLXUw"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b00942</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MnFe2O4@C Nanofibers as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Yu, Chuanming; Jiao, Lifang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3321-3328</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnFe2O4 nanodots (∼3.3 nm) homogeneously dispersed in porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (denoted as MFO@C) were prepd. by a feasible electrospinning technique.  Meanwhile, MFO@C with the character of flexible free-standing membrane was directly used as binder- and current collector-free anode for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting high electrochem. performance with high-rate capability (305 mA h g-1 at 10000 mA g-1 in comparison of 504 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1) and ultralong cycling life (ca. 90% capacity retention after 4200 cycles).  The Na-storage mechanism was systematically studied, revealing that MnFe2O4 is converted into metallic Mn and Fe after the first discharge (MnFe2O4 + 8Na+ + 8e- → Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O) and then to MnO and Fe2O3 during the following charge (Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O → MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e-).  The subsequent cycles occur through reversible redox reactions of MnO + Fe2O3 + 8Na+ + 8e- &lt;-&gt; Mn + 2Fe + 4Na2O, of which the redn./oxidn. of MnO/Mn takes place at a lower potential than that of Fe2O3/Fe.  Furthermore, a soft package sodium-ion full battery with MFO@C anode and Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode was assembled, delivering a stable capacity of ∼400 mA h g-1 for MFO@C (with 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1) and a promising energy d. of 77.8 Wh kg-1 for the whole battery.  This is owing to the distinctive structure of very-fine MnFe2O4 nanodots embedded in porous N-doped carbon nanofibers, which effectively improves the utilization rate of active materials, facilitates the transportation of electrons and Na+ ions, and prevents the particle pulverization/agglomeration upon prolonged cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo_fovS2KMexbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgT8AA11eLXUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XlsFKqtLk%253D&amp;md5=1f0fa2211d961158137c8cc4eb8fdd4c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Henderson, W. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sushko, M. L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Engelhard, M.                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.10.034</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard carbon nanoparticles as high-capacity, high-stability anodic materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Lifen; Cao, Yuliang; Henderson, Wesley A.; Sushko, Maria L.; Shao, Yuyan; Xiao, Jie; Wang, Wei; Engelhard, Mark H.; Nie, Zimin; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">279-288</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon nanoparticles (HCNP) were synthesized by the pyrolysis of a polyaniline precursor.  The measured Na+ cation diffusion coeff. (10-13-10-15 cm2 s-1) in the HCNP obtained at 1150 °C is two orders of magnitude lower than that of Li+ in graphite (10-10-10-13 cm2 s-1), indicating that reducing the carbon particle size is very important for improving electrochem. performance.  These measurements also enable a clear visualization of the stepwise reaction phases and rate changes which occur throughout the insertion/extn. processes in HCNP, The electrochem. measurements also show that the nano-sized HCNP obtained at 1150 °C exhibited higher practical capacity at voltages lower than 1.2 V (vs. Na/Na+), as well as a prolonged cycling stability, which is attributed to an optimum spacing of 0.366 nm between the graphitic layers and the nano particular size resulting in a low-barrier Na+ cation insertion.  These results suggest that HCNP is a very promising high-capacity/stability anode for low cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0215ZE-6YJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgT8AA11eLXUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVaqtrrE&amp;md5=93cb764059ea5aaa3841222611c03416</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00744B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controllable Synthesis of Mn<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Nanodots@Nitrogen-Doped Graphene and its Application for High Energy Density Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         rightTab-cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable synthesis of Mn3O4 nanodots@nitrogen-doped graphene and its application for high energy density supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Li; Su, Lijun; Lang, Junwei; Hu, Bin; Xu, Shan; Yan, Xingbin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5523-5531</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Supercapacitors using ionic liqs. (ILs) as electrolytes have triggered great interest due to their much higher energy d. when compared to aq. supercapacitors.  Although Mn oxides have obvious capacitive contribution in ILs and thus can be used as electrode materials for IL-based supercapacitors, they suffer from low specific capacitance in ILs.  Here, Mn3O4 nanodots loaded on N-doped graphene sheets (denoted as Mn3O4 NDs@NG) are prepd. through a facile 1-pot solvothermal method with the presence of octylamine as the surfactant.  Octylamine plays an important role in obtaining quantum-sized Mn3O4 NDs and controlling their dispersion degree on the surface of NG.  With an optimal loading mass of Mn3O4 NDs, the corresponding Mn3O4 NDs@NG material is able to achieve a high specific capacitance of 158.9 F/g in a given IL and shows excellent rate capability.  On this basis, a sym. supercapacitor is assembled based on such a Mn3O4 NDs@NG, which delivers a high energy d. of 90.7 Wh/Kg in the IL electrolyte.  An asym. supercapacitor is also built using such a Mn3O4 NDs@NG and activated C as the neg. and pos. electrode, resp.  This asym. device shows a higher energy d. of 124.4 Wh/Kg compared to the sym. one, and it still can deliver 55.8 Wh/Kg at a large power d. of 29.9 KW/Kg.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpO5FCFs3o5MrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgT8AA11eLXUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXis1WktL0%253D&amp;md5=50268d34f4d3e6e310ebc6d06140560c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref52" class="rightTabRefNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit52" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201601959"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bu, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Olive-shaped anatase TiO2 with tunable sizes in nanoscale are designed employing polyvinyl alc. (PVA) as structure directing agents to impact on structure shaping and size manipulation.  Notably, the introduced PVA simultaneously serves as C sources, bringing about a homogeneous C layer with intimate coupling interfaces for boosted electronic cond.  Constructed from tiny cryst. grains, the uniformly dispersed C-coated TiO2 nano-olives (TOC) possess subtle loose structure internally for prompt Na+ transportation.  When used for Na-ion storage, the size effects are increasingly significant at high charge-discharge rates, leading to the much superior rate performances of TOC with the smallest size.  Bestowed by the improved Na+ adsorption and diffusion kinetics together with the promoted electron transfer, it delivers a high specific capacity of 267 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C (33.6 mA g-1) and sustains 110 mA h g-1 at a rather high rate of 20 C.  Even after cycled at 10 C over 1000 cycles, a considerable capacity of 125 mA h g-1 with a retention of 94.6% is still obtained, highlighting its long-term cyclability and high-rate capabilities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsTZm-u-NF0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgT8AA11eLXUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVChtbzF&amp;md5=f143b6730d4e33771e789c43b778393f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1039/C7CC00087A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MnOOH Nanorods as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnOOH nanorods, which were prepd. using a hydrothermal method, have been used for the first time as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  The as-prepd. MnOOH nanorods with lengths of 1.2-3.7 μm and diams. of 60-90 nm delivered high performance of reversible electrochem. Na/Na+ storage such as an initial discharge capacity of 485.5 mA h g-1 at 80 mA g-1, a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 86.7% and a low av. potential polarization of 0.36 V.  Instrumental analyses with ex situ XRD, TEM and XPS show that the sodium storage mechanism in MnOOH can be related to the reversible formation of MnO and NaOH.  This work demonstrates that cheap MnOOH nanorods are potential anode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0RnhEy9Fg6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgT8AA11eLXUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvF2hur8%253D&amp;md5=336562e3da2cc591a2a5bc20b4cc014e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201603716"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Ribbon Assembled Core-Sheath MnO@Graphene Scrolls as Hierarchically Ordered 3D Porous Electrodes for Fast and Durable Lithium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Ribbon Assembled Core-Sheath MnO@Graphene Scrolls as Hierarchically Ordered 3D Porous Electrodes for Fast and Durable Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yun; Chen, Penghui; Gao, Xu; Wang, Bo; Liu, Heng; Wu, Hao; Liu, Huakun; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7754-7765</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene scroll is an emerging 1D tubular form of graphitic carbon that has potential applications in electrochem. energy storage.  However, it still remains a challenge to composite graphene scrolls with other nanomaterials for building advanced electrode configuration with fast and durable lithium storage properties.  Here, a transition-metal-oxide-based hierarchically ordered 3D porous electrode is designed based on assembling 1D core-sheath MnO@N-doped graphene scrolls with 2D N-doped graphene ribbons.  In the resulting architecture, porous MnO nanowires confined in tubular graphene scrolls are mech. isolated but electronically well-connected, while the interwoven graphene ribbons offer continuous conductive paths for electron transfer in all directions.  Moreover, the elastic graphene scrolls together with enough internal voids are able to accommodate the vol. expansion of the enclosed MnO.  Because of these merits, the as-built electrode manifests ultrahigh rate capability (349 mAh g-1 at 8.0 A g-1; 205 mAh g-1 at 15.0 A g-1) and robust cycling stability (812 mAh g-1 remaining after 1000 cycles at 2.0 A g-1) and is the most efficient MnO-based anode ever reported for lithium-ion batteries.  This unique multidimensional and hierarchically ordered structure design is believed to hold great potential in generalizable synthesis of graphene scrolls composited with oxide nanowires for mutifuctional energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh8xcBh8-tE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9AavxFLYf3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFenu7%252FM&amp;md5=632f9f9db962b375bfe78764a2077cd9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref57" class="rightTabRefNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit57" data-doi="10.1016/S0378-7753(99)00180-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Takeda, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Imanishi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ichikawa, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yamamoto, O.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Study of the Cycling Performance of Finely Dispersed Lithium Alloy Composite Electrodes under High Li-Utilization</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) derived transition metal oxides exhibit enhanced performance in energy conversion and storage.  In this work, porous hollow Co3O4 with N-doped carbon coating (Co3O4/N-C) polyhedrons have been prepd. using cobalt-based MOFs as a sacrificial template.  Assembled from tiny nanoparticles and N-doped carbon coating, Co3O4/N-C composite shortens the diffusion length of Li+/Na+ ions and possesses an enhanced cond.  The porous and hollow structure is also beneficial for tolerating vol. changes in the galvanostatic discharge/charge cycles as lithium/sodium battery anode materials.  As a result, it can exhibit impressive cycling and rating performance.  At 1000 mA g-1, the specific capacities maintained stable values of ∼620 mAh g-1 within 2000 cycles as anodes in lithium ion battery, while the specific capacity keeps at 229 mAh g-1 within 150 cycles as sodium ion battery anode.  The work shows comparable cycling performance in lithium ion battery but even better high-rate cycling stability as sodium ion battery anode.  Herein, a facile method is provided to construct high electrochem. performance oxide/N-C composite electrode using new MOFs as sacrificial template.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohdLj6rKhXM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9AavxFLYf3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXktV2lurc%253D&amp;md5=59b9e06ccf54aa8f4145800d531cb607</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref62" class="rightTabRefNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit62" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b05041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zou, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ni-based metal org. frameworks (Ni-MOFs) with unique hierarchical hollow ball-in-ball nanostructure were synthesized by solvothermal reactions.  After successive carbonization and oxidn. treatments, hierarchical NiO/Ni nanocrystals covered with a graphene shell were obtained with the hollow ball-in-ball nanostructure intact.  The resulting materials exhibited superior performance as the anode in lithium ion batteries (LIBs): they provide high reversible specific capacity (1144 mAh/g), excellent cyclability (nearly no capacity loss after 1000 cycles) and rate performance (805 mAh/g at 15 A/g). Such a superior lithium and sodium storage performance is derived from the well-designed hierarchical hollow ball-in-ball structure of NiO/Ni/Graphene composites, which not only mitigates the vol. expansion of NiO during the cycles but also provides a continuous highly conductive graphene matrix to facilitate the fast charge transfer and form a stable SEI layer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFsltJ-ZhbyLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9AavxFLYf3w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFSmtbzM&amp;md5=98be0e8818487e6970ee353c03aa159e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref63" class="rightTabRefNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit63" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b11238"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospinning Synthesis of Mesoporous MnCoNiO<sub>x</sub>@Double-Carbon Nanofibers for Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes with Pseudocapacitive Behavior and Long Cycle Life</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.
